The air under the center of that long deck lid is bad. Air moving over the body creates a low-pressure area in the middle of the backend. This becomes a big problem at speeds over 300, but it can happen at speeds less than that under the right conditions. This is why we experimented with chute placement on funny cars in the late 90s. Moving the chutes to positions on the outside of the rear deck will fix the problem. The air on the outside of the body is cleaner and gives the chutes a better chance to develop without getting tangled.

You know I used to skydive, okay? And I packed my own primary shoot, basically from the beginning.  But I always had my reserve packed by professional.  And whenever he was in the building, I would have him observe me packing my primary to make sure that I was doing things correctly.  It may be time to add a third parachute to mullet.  Simply so, you can be at a very high probability of at least two deploying.  Maybe the third parachute would be a reserve that is not packed by you, but is packed by someone else, and you only deploy that parachute in the event of something scary.  I also have suggested this before, but I didn't see any kind of reaction on it. You might want to look into sliders.  Sliders delay and slow the opening of parachutes.  I know that sounds counterintuitive, but it would greatly improve the controllability of the car as the parachutes are  I've seen several times it looked very scary because of the way that your pair shoots deploy and the way it jerks around the back of the car. Now, I am not a drag racer, never done that. So I really don't know a lot about that. I do know something about skydiving and sliders when appropriately used really do make a difference in both reducing the impact of Shoot opening, improving controllability and reducing the number of tangles and other malfunctions because of rapid  Also, reduces damage to the parachute itself.  Now, I don't know if sliders are applicable in drag racing, that might be something you want to look into.  There may be a good reason that they're not used. I don't know.
